  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_859f113e-07d9-4d47-935d-404e860339b9'

Now—in his wife’s honor—he decides to continue a very special search. But in the process he makes a critical mistake and one of his daughters stumbles onto a letter she was never supposed to see.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1886697897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9577903295221649851">I return to this series when I need a wholesome break from contemporary literary fiction with all of its dysfunction and navel-gazing. Maybe I'm old-fashioned, but I relate much more to these normal characters trying to live good lives than to many of the characters in the books featured in the NY Times Book Review. These books are clean soap operas - pure escapism.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2402692988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2402692988" />
    <a title="Stefanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64200589-stefanie"><img alt="Stefanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595957756p2/64200589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2402692988?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefanie" href="/user/show/64200589-stefanie">Stefanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2402692988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8465505977337464154">Karen Kingsbury’s second novel in the Firstborn series is a beautiful story on forgiveness. It will tug at your heartstrings as the characters, Katy and Dayne, try to maneuver through some tricky, emotional, messes. And the Baxter family? Yeah, the Baxter family is full of love and life and I can’t get enough of them. You fall in love with each member of that family as if they are truly part of your own. More drama unfolds in this novel, Forgiven, as it leads into what book three has in store. L</span>
  <span id="freeText8465505977337464154" style="display:none">Karen Kingsbury’s second novel in the Firstborn series is a beautiful story on forgiveness. It will tug at your heartstrings as the characters, Katy and Dayne, try to maneuver through some tricky, emotional, messes. And the Baxter family? Yeah, the Baxter family is full of love and life and I can’t get enough of them. You fall in love with each member of that family as if they are truly part of your own. More drama unfolds in this novel, Forgiven, as it leads into what book three has in store. Looking forward to it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8465505977337464154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10485243305324058852" style="display:none">Karen is just messing with my feelings and she’s so good at that. But she’s also kind of cruel.<br />My point is: this book/this series might not be like the greatest or finest piece of literature out there and the translation definitely wasn’t one of the bests, but the way the author managed to express the characters’ feelings and how she put things head to head it’s amazing. I’m so curious about how things will fall into place eventually and I’m sure it’s going to be awesome and not what I expected.<br />And last, but not least, I wanted to say a little bit about the way Karen pictured different characters in their relationship with God. Like in the “Redemption” series, she just pointed out so many scenarios and so many possibilities and how she managed to highlight God’s purpose and plans for these people is just amazing and I love the message in this book in particular. A message of forgiveness, love instead of hate and peace instead of chaos.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2195974921?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Marie" href="/user/show/11986319-anne-marie">Anne Marie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2195974921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8282236423865749027">This book continued to focus mainly on Dayne Matthews and his life of stardom and always being followed by paparazzi. He is making a movie that originally would have had him starring with Katy Hart. But after the incident with the crazed stalker Katy is happily back in Bloomington directing Christian Kids Theater. The next play is Annie and auditions for parts are taking place. Dayne will be starring in the movie with his live-in girlfriend, Kelly Parker. <br/>After a day of auditions and working on </span>
  <span id="freeText8282236423865749027" style="display:none">This book continued to focus mainly on Dayne Matthews and his life of stardom and always being followed by paparazzi. He is making a movie that originally would have had him starring with Katy Hart. But after the incident with the crazed stalker Katy is happily back in Bloomington directing Christian Kids Theater. The next play is Annie and auditions for parts are taking place. Dayne will be starring in the movie with his live-in girlfriend, Kelly Parker. <br />After a day of auditions and working on the play takes place, a tragic accident involving a mom and four children occurs. A drunk driver, Jeremy Fisher, hits the van, killing a young boy and Sarah Jo Stryker, a girl with a beautiful voice that would have brought her many lead rolls in future plays. The children at Christian Kids Theater learn a valuable lesson in forgiveness over time by going to Bible studies and<br />talking about life’s tragedies with Katy. They even visit the prison and get to talk to Jeremy. <br />Dayne Matthews can’t get Katy Hart out of his mind. He’s living with his leading actress in his current movie, and thinking about joining a new religion, Kabbalah. When he goes to Bloomington a few days early before filming begins, he rekindles a relationship with Katy. Katy is starting to have feelings for Dayne as well. But they come from two different worlds, and Katy still feels any type of relationship couldn’t work. But Katy does meet with Dayne one last time to give him information about Kabbalah saying it’s not right for him. She also gives him a piece of advice...read the note his biological mother left on a picture he has of her. It’s a good place to start with his spiritual journey. Dayne takes her advice when he gets back to Hollywood. He no longer is interested in Kabbalah. Reading his mother’s note on her picture makes Dayne want to be a better person, maybe even following God. He keeps his promise of being at Bloomington for the opening of the Annie play. Unfortunately, he has no time to talk to Katy or he’ll miss his flight back. <br />Dayne at least sees Katy as well as his sisters. He doesn’t think he’ll ever let them know that he is their brother. It would be too complicated, and the paparazzi could mess up the Baxter family’s private lives. <br />Brooke’s daughter Hayley continues to get better from her drowning. She is now walking with a walker! <br />Kari and Ryan help Ashley and Landon paint sets for the play. <br />Ashley finds a letter in her dad’s room marked “Firstborn.” Even though her dad told her not to bother the letters, that he would make copies for all the kids, Ashley thinks she could do her father a favor and give the letter to her oldest sister, Brooke. But when curiosity has her open and read the letter, she finds out the secret her parents have never told the family. Her parents gave up a son before they were married. <br />Erin and Luke are still living in Texas and New York. They try to keep in touch with the family as much as possible. <br />John Baxter has been enjoying his friendship with Elaine Denning, a widow. They go to the farmer’s market every Saturday and John confides his secret to her about his firstborn son. After Ashley finds the letter her mother wrote and talks to her father, they both agree not to tell anyone until the whole family is together for spring break. <br />The Flanigan family, with its six children, is becoming an important fixture in Bloomington. Bailey and her brother Connor are involved in CKT. Jenny and her husband Jim try to be good listeners and guide Katy and their children in the right direction with their lives. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3481304517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3481304517" />
    <a title="Jack Vasen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52966326-jack-vasen"><img alt="Jack Vasen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456179595p2/52966326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3481304517?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Vasen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Vasen" href="/user/show/52966326-jack-vasen">Jack Vasen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966326-jack-vasen?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966326-jack-vasen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966326-jack-vasen?shelf=series-must-read-all">series-must-read-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3481304517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13926118015543233732">This series is mostly one long story which is built upon characters developed in a previous series (The Redemption Collection). This book almost tells a complete story but there are such obvious unresolved threads that finishing this book alone is unsatisfying. This is definitely a series to be read in order. As to characters from the previous series, the author fills us in on the important details, but as I was reading, I definitely realized I was missing something since I had not read the earl</span>
  <span id="freeText13926118015543233732" style="display:none">This series is mostly one long story which is built upon characters developed in a previous series (The Redemption Collection). This book almost tells a complete story but there are such obvious unresolved threads that finishing this book alone is unsatisfying. This is definitely a series to be read in order. As to characters from the previous series, the author fills us in on the important details, but as I was reading, I definitely realized I was missing something since I had not read the earlier books.<br /><br />The title says it all. The story is actually mostly predictable, some things more easily than others. It is a remarkable and touching story. As I often do with books where God plays such a significant role, I wish it were a true story or based on one because a human author can play god, but only the true God can make things like this really happen.<br /><br />Meanwhile, the author is a tease. The book is filled little teases. There are chapters that end in suspense while the next one starts somewhere else. There are chance meetings that are momentous but that isn't recognized by the characters at this point in the story. In a similar way there are statements and thoughts by characters that they have no idea how they are either completely untrue or at other times prophetic. There's love that seems to have no hope.<br /><br />There are a lot of characters and a lot of story threads. Most of them revolve around Dayne and his unknowing biological family.<br /><br />The climax is quite moving.<br /><br />This is a Christian book. Kingsbury often uses actions of characters to preach rather than words, but in this book she uses both.<br /><br />Mature themes: there is no sex described although it is implied in some cases. There is a very tragic auto accident with devastating effects that occupy much of the story. There's drug use and alcoholism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13926118015543233732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3074871380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3074871380" />
    <a title="Rana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88119541-rana"><img alt="Rana" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3074871380?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rana" href="/user/show/88119541-rana">Rana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3074871380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3034466452995722845">I really like all the Baxter series that I've read so far (Redemption Series #1-5 & now the first two of the Firstborn series). The author does a great job of showing how a person's decisions affect not only themselves but others as well. I like how when she chooses a theme for a book--not just one character goes through a lesson on this theme so do others--sometimes a whole group of people. Like in this book#2 the theme was about forgiveness. MANY people had to learn about this topic from varyi</span>
  <span id="freeText3034466452995722845" style="display:none">I really like all the Baxter series that I've read so far (Redemption Series #1-5 &amp; now the first two of the Firstborn series). The author does a great job of showing how a person's decisions affect not only themselves but others as well. I like how when she chooses a theme for a book--not just one character goes through a lesson on this theme so do others--sometimes a whole group of people. Like in this book#2 the theme was about forgiveness. MANY people had to learn about this topic from varying viewpoints. Sometimes the theme is shown from a saved character's viewpoint and sometimes from an unsaved person's viewpoint. Sometimes they are a mature believer fleshing out their beliefs and sometimes they are a less mature believer who is struggling to learn how to trust God and grow &amp; learn from a more mature believer. Life isn't easy for ANY of her characters--they ALL have to make some tough choices &amp; live with the consequences of their actions--much like we all have to do whether we are saved or not. I find her writing relateable, enjoyable, encouraging &amp; inspiring to grow me in my own faith. The answers, though not easy, can always be found in God, His Word, through prayer &amp; results in peace that comes from handling everything we go through His way. Even when God's ways are not initially chosen--when the character returns to God/finds Him for the first time-- the wrongs can be redeemable &amp; can still be used for good in that person's life--just as it is in real life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3034466452995722845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1393780071?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taryn Spearey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taryn Spearey" href="/user/show/43487135-taryn-spearey">Taryn Spearey</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2997388198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16264828801799239231">Kingsbury is a very predictable writer, but that doesn't stop me from anxiously awaiting to see how each story unfolds! This book had me crying then laughing. I love how Kingsbury takes real life issues and turns them into a shining light for God's love. A few editorial critiques...why does she list every character as their first and last name every time they enter the story? It gets very repetitive! Also, does Katy not have parents of her own? It would be nice if she had a sounding board to tal</span>
  <span id="freeText16264828801799239231" style="display:none">Kingsbury is a very predictable writer, but that doesn't stop me from anxiously awaiting to see how each story unfolds! This book had me crying then laughing. I love how Kingsbury takes real life issues and turns them into a shining light for God's love. A few editorial critiques...why does she list every character as their first and last name every time they enter the story? It gets very repetitive! Also, does Katy not have parents of her own? It would be nice if she had a sounding board to talk things over with. Rhonda is her best friend, but she never gets real or deep with her. I know there's no way to resolve these critiques, but they keep coming to mind whenever I pick back up in the series. Overall, great quality read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16264828801799239231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XyblJ//D0hMmejvaLlIbWiKSRDG0935XLJlKysVO/Jjj+RotB5gvXV+RGAoLpjJpl8+ld/BV+0aYbyr12Zut7g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3/8Uo39qH5Lkfe2ZuJt9m8XtzfAr9n6yKVnK09s5zP9jIOuphzHi3J2Wzkmdb1SocLAstm9U+6Odr6rsx+ydiQ==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText17875182107141743386" style="display:none">Karen Kingsbury, #1 New York Times bestselling novelist, is America’s favorite inspirational storyteller, with more than twenty-five million copies of her award-winning books in print. Her last dozen titles have topped bestseller lists and many of her novels are under development with Hallmark Films and as major motion pictures. Her Baxter Family books are being developed into a TV series slated for major network viewing sometime in the next year. Karen is also an adjunct professor of writing at Liberty University. In 2001 she and her husband, Don, adopted three boys from Haiti, doubling their family in a matter of months.
